        // Disable analytics when hit from DD synthetics browser
        if (window._DATADOG_SYNTHETICS_BROWSER === undefined) {
          if (window.initialStoreData && window.initialStoreData.userInfo.meta

                dataLayer.push({learningAccountType: 'individual'});

                dataLayer.push({learningAccountType: 'free trial'});

                dataLayer.push({learningAccountType: 'academic'});

              }
            }

            // Set paid account
            if (user.subscription && user.subscription.active) {
              dataLayer.push({ learningPaidAccount: 'yes' });
            }
          }

css-zv7ju9" role="main" id="main" data-testid="muiShellMain"><div class="" style="display:flex;flex-direction:row;height:100%;overflow:hidden;width:100%" data-panel-group="" data-panel-group-direction="horizontal" data-panel-group-id=":R5b:"><div class="_panel_54vr9_17" id="content-panel" style="flex: 1 1 0px; overflow: hidden;" data-panel="" data-panel-group-id=":R5b:" data-panel-id="content-panel" data-panel-size="1.0"><section class="_contentContainer_8mmlj_34 _white_8mmlj_146 ucvMode-white ucvFamily-Serif _sidebarIsOpen_8mmlj_51"><article class="_contentSection_8mmlj_56"><section data-testid="contentViewer" class="_contentViewer_1idwi_1"><div class="_annotatable_dsxx3_1"><div id="book-content" class="noOutline" tabindex="-1"><link rel="stylesheet" href="./1.Understanding CI_CD _ CI_CD Pipeline Using Jenkins Unleashed_ Solutions While Setting Up CI_CD Processes_files/override_v1.css" crossorigin="anonymous"><style class="darkreader darkreader--sync" media="screen"></style><link rel="stylesheet" href="./1.Understanding CI_CD _ CI_CD Pipeline Using Jenkins Unleashed_ Solutions While Setting Up CI_CD Processes_files/springer_epub.css" crossorigin="anonymous"><style class="darkreader darkreader--sync" media="screen"></style><div class="orm-ChapterReader-readerContainer orm-ChapterReader-white" style="font-size: 1.3em; max-width: 70ch;"><div id="sbo-rt-content"><div epub:type="chapter" role="doc-chapter"><div class="ChapterContextInformation"><div class="ContextInformation" id="b978-1-4842-7508-5_1"><div class="ChapterCopyright">&nbsp;The Author(s), under exclusive license to APress Media, LLC, part of Springer Nature&nbsp;2022</div><span class="ContextInformationAuthorEditorNames">P. P. Dingare</span><span class="ContextInformationBookTitles"><span class="BookTitle">CI/CD Pipeline Using Jenkins Unleashed</span></span><span class="ChapterDOI"><a href="https://doi.org/10.1007/978-1-4842-7508-5_1" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">https://doi.org/10.1007/978-1-4842-7508-5_1</a></span></div></div><div class="MainTitleSection"><h1 class="ChapterTitle" lang="en">1.&nbsp;Understanding CI/CD</h1></div><div class="AuthorGroup"><div class="AuthorNames"><span class="Author"><span class="AuthorName">Pranoday&nbsp;Pramod&nbsp;Dingare</span><sup><a href="https://learning.oreilly.com/library/view/ci-cd-pipeline-using/9781484275085/html/515276_1_En_1_Chapter.xhtml#Aff2" aria-label="Footnote 1">1</a>&nbsp;<span class="ContactIcon">&nbsp;</span></sup></span></div><div class="Affiliations"><div class="Affiliation" id="Aff2"><span class="AffiliationNumber">(1)</span><div class="AffiliationText">Pune, Maharashtra, India</div></div><div class="ClearBoth">&nbsp;</div></div></div><div class="Fulltext"><p class="Para" id="Par2">This chapter explains what CI/CD is in practice and how it has influenced software development in general. In modern-day application development processes, where the Agile development lifecycle is used, its common to have frequent changes to the application code.</p><div class="FormalPara FormalParaRenderingStyle1 ParaTypeImportant" id="FPar1"><div class="Heading">Note</div><p class="Para FirstParaInFormalPara" id="Par3">Agile is a development lifecycle model in which each member of the development team (i.e., the developers, testers, business analysts, etc.) works on the same set of requirements at the same time. In other development lifecycle models, such as <span id="ITerm1">Rapid Application Development (RAD)</span>, different people work on different requirements. For example, the software testers work on a piece of functionality that the developers have finished working on, and the developers might be developing requirements that the business analysts have completed.</p></div><p class="Para" id="Par4">In the <span id="ITerm2">Agile development lifecycle model</span>, application requirements are divided into multiple sets of prioritized requirements, which are taken up for implementation as part of the application development process. A <em class="EmphasisTypeItalic ">sprint</em> is a timeframe within which a single set of requirements is worked on, from the phase of requirements review until their final implementation in an application.</p><p class="Para" id="Par5">In Agile, the application evolves with every sprint. A sprint, which usually spans one to three weeks, adds a considerable amount of functionality in a short period. In a single day, multiple developers working on an application will complete development of assigned functionalities and will commit their changes to the main branch. (The code from this branch is used to create a build; its usually a master branch in the case of GitLab and a main branch in the case of GitHub.) This practice of merging all the changes at once can introduce problems, like regression defects, integration defects, and merge conflicts, and these problems can take hours to find and resolve.</p><p class="Para" id="Par6">To avoid these problems, <span id="ITerm3"><em class="EmphasisTypeItalic ">Continuous Integration (CI)</em></span> is practiced in <span id="ITerm4">Agile methodology</span>. In CI, work completed by the developers is merged frequently into the main branch, rather than waiting until the end of the day or until the end of the sprint. This practice of merging fewer changes at a time allows developers to resolve merge conflicts earlier and address regression defects more efficiently and quickly.</p><section class="Section1 RenderAsSection1" id="Sec1"><h2 class="Heading">The Development Workflow</h2><section class="Section2 RenderAsSection2" id="Sec2"><h3 class="Heading">Running Unit Tests Locally</h3><p class="Para" id="Par7">The developer obtains their own copy of the latest code from the central repository and implements the required <span id="ITerm5">changes</span>. These changes are usually implemented using test-driven development practices. The development and changes to the code continue until all written unit test cases pass.</p><div class="FormalPara FormalParaRenderingStyle1 ParaTypeImportant" id="FPar2"><div class="Heading">Note</div><p class="Para FirstParaInFormalPara" id="Par8"><span id="ITerm6">Test-driven development (TDD)</span> is a practice in which test cases are written before developing the code. Written test cases are executed, which will fail as there is no code written as per the expectations prescribed in the test case. Then the code is developed to fulfill the test cases expectations.</p></div></section><section class="Section2 RenderAsSection2" id="Sec3"><h3 class="Heading">Pushing and Merging Code to the Central Repository</h3><p class="Para" id="Par9">Once the developers finish the development work in the local copy, they push this <span id="ITerm7">code to the central repository</span> to be merged into the main branch.</p></section><section class="Section2 RenderAsSection2" id="Sec4"><h3 class="Heading">Compiling Code after the Merge</h3><p class="Para" id="Par10">Once the developers code is merged with the main branch, this merged code must be compiled. This reveals any new compilation errors that were introduced due to merging the newly developed code with the existing code.</p></section><section class="Section2 RenderAsSection2" id="Sec5"><h3 class="Heading">Running Tests on the Merged Code</h3><p class="Para" id="Par11">After a successful merger, the <span id="ITerm8">unit and integration tests</span> are executed to reveal any regression defects. In addition to these, a few CI processes encourage static analysis to be executed on the code to check for adherence to the coding standards, existence of dead code, and so on.</p></section><section class="Section2 RenderAsSection2" id="Sec6"><h3 class="Heading">Deploying an Artifact</h3><p class="Para" id="Par12">Once the merged code is checked against the various quality attributes, an artifact is built and deployed to the deployment server. All <span id="ITerm9">stable code</span> is packed and deployed to the server for the end users to use. These artifacts take the form of .WAR or.JAR files, for example.</p></section></section><section class="Section1 RenderAsSection1" id="Sec7"><h2 class="Heading">Continuous Delivery/Continuous Deployment</h2><p class="Para" id="Par13">In Continuous <span id="ITerm10">Integration</span>, incremental changes to the application are tested in a development environment, which reveals any failures. Once the changes are tested and confirmed in the development environment, including these changes in periodic builds is very important.</p><p class="Para" id="Par14">It may happen that the application is working fine in the development environment, but having problems in the production environment. These problems could be because a new change is not compatible with the hardware/software in the production environment. If the application is not frequently deployed in the production environment, then debugging and resolving such problems could turn out to be a nightmare.</p></section><section class="Section1 RenderAsSection1" id="Sec8"><h2 class="Heading">CI/CD Workflow Case Study</h2><p class="Para" id="Par15">For this case study, youll develop a <span id="ITerm11">Calculator Web application</span> that includes addition, subtraction, multiplication, and division functionalities.</p><section class="Section2 RenderAsSection2" id="Sec9"><h3 class="Heading">Pulling the Applications Latest Code</h3><p class="Para" id="Par16">Youll pull the latest application code on the local machine from a central code repository to start developing the addition functionality. It will add two numbers and return the result.</p></section><section class="Section2 RenderAsSection2" id="Sec10"><h3 class="Heading">Developing and Running Unit Test Cases</h3><p class="Para" id="Par17">You will develop unit test <span id="ITerm12">cases</span> before you start writing the code. You will execute the written unit test cases, which will fail, as there is no code written to satisfy the expectations mentioned in the test cases.</p><div class="Para" id="Par18">For example, calling <span class="EmphasisFontCategoryNonProportional ">Addition(10,20)</span> and comparing the return value with <span class="EmphasisFontCategoryNonProportional ">30</span> to confirm the addition functionality works fine. See Listing <span class="InternalRef"><a href="https://learning.oreilly.com/library/view/ci-cd-pipeline-using/9781484275085/html/515276_1_En_1_Chapter.xhtml#PC1">1-1</a></span>.<div class="ProgramCode" id="PC1"><div class="LineGroup"><div class="FixedLine">{</div><div class="FixedLine">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Result=Addition(10,20);</div><div class="FixedLine">Assert.assertEquals(Result,30,"Addition functionality does not work fine with positive numbers");</div><div class="FixedLine">}</div></div><div class="Caption" lang="en"><div class="CaptionContent"><span class="CaptionNumber">Listing 1-1</span><p class="SimplePara">Unit Test Case for the Addition Functionality</p></div></div></div></div><p class="Para" id="Par19">This test code calls an <span class="EmphasisFontCategoryNonProportional ">Addition</span> function with two positive numbers, 10 and 20. It receives the result in the <span class="EmphasisFontCategoryNonProportional ">Result</span> variable and compares the value in the <span class="EmphasisFontCategoryNonProportional ">Result</span> variable with <span class="EmphasisFontCategoryNonProportional ">30</span>. If the <span class="EmphasisFontCategoryNonProportional ">Result</span> variable contains the value 30, the test case will be marked as <span class="EmphasisFontCategoryNonProportional ">Passed</span>. Otherwise, it is marked as <span class="EmphasisFontCategoryNonProportional ">Failed</span>.</p><p class="Para" id="Par20">This test case fails with the error <span class="EmphasisFontCategoryNonProportional ">Addition(10,20) function does not exist</span> (we do not have a function called <span class="EmphasisFontCategoryNonProportional ">Addition()</span> yet). In test-driven development, the test cases should fail first until the developer develops the functionality with the intention of making the failed tests pass.</p><div class="FormalPara FormalParaRenderingStyle1 ParaTypeImportant" id="FPar3"><div class="Heading">Note</div><p class="Para FirstParaInFormalPara" id="Par21">We dont assume the use of any particular language or unit testing tool here. For now, concentrate on understanding the concept and flow of CI/CD instead of getting into the details of language and specific tools</p></div></section><section class="Section2 RenderAsSection2" id="Sec11"><h3 class="Heading">Code Development</h3><div class="Para" id="Par22">To make the failed test case pass, you must implement the <span class="EmphasisFontCategoryNonProportional ">Addition</span> <span id="ITerm13">function</span>, as shown in Listing <span class="InternalRef"><a href="https://learning.oreilly.com/library/view/ci-cd-pipeline-using/9781484275085/html/515276_1_En_1_Chapter.xhtml#PC2">1-2</a></span>.<div class="ProgramCode" id="PC2"><div class="LineGroup"><div class="FixedLine">Addition(a,b)</div><div class="FixedLine">{</div><div class="FixedLine">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Result=a+b;</div><div class="FixedLine">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;return Result;</div><div class="FixedLine">}</div></div><div class="Caption" lang="en"><div class="CaptionContent"><span class="CaptionNumber">Listing 1-2</span><p class="SimplePara">Code for the Addition <span id="ITerm14">Functionality</span></p></div></div></div></div><p class="Para" id="Par23">Along with this backend code, component changes would also be made to the frontend code. For example, an Addition pushbutton would be added to the UI to trigger this function.</p></section><section class="Section2 RenderAsSection2" id="Sec12"><h3 class="Heading">Rerunning the Unit Test Case</h3><p class="Para" id="Par24">If you <span id="ITerm15">rerun the unit test case</span>, it will now pass.</p></section><section class="Section2 RenderAsSection2" id="Sec13"><h3 class="Heading">Pushing and Merging the Code to the Central Repository</h3><p class="Para" id="Par25">You can now push the <span class="EmphasisFontCategoryNonProportional ">Addition</span> function code to the central repository to be merged with rest of the applications code.</p></section><section class="Section2 RenderAsSection2" id="Sec14"><h3 class="Heading">Compiling the Code after the Merge</h3><p class="Para" id="Par26">After the <span id="ITerm16"><span class="EmphasisFontCategoryNonProportional ">Addition()</span> function code</span> is merged, the whole application will be compiled.</p></section><section class="Section2 RenderAsSection2" id="Sec15"><h3 class="Heading">Running Tests on the Merged Code</h3><p class="Para" id="Par27">A few integration tests and tests related to other functionalities like subtraction, multiplication, and so on, will be executed to confirm that this newly added <span class="EmphasisFontCategoryNonProportional ">Addition</span> functionality has not broken any previous functionalities.</p></section><section class="Section2 RenderAsSection2" id="Sec16"><h3 class="Heading">Deploying an Artifact</h3><p class="Para" id="Par28">Now you build the <span id="ITerm17">web application and deploy</span> it in the production environment on an application server (e.g., tomcat).</p></section><section class="Section2 RenderAsSection2" id="Sec17"><h3 class="Heading">Run e-e Tests on a Deployed Application</h3><p class="Para" id="Par29">Finally, you need to <span id="ITerm18">run e-e tests</span> using UI automation tools like Selenium and confirm that the applications end-end flows are working fine.</p></section></section><section class="Section1 RenderAsSection1" id="Sec18"><h2 class="Heading">Summary</h2><p class="Para" id="Par30">This chapter explained the problems of following traditional development processes in a fast-paced development model like Agile. This chapter also explained how you can benefit from adopting CI/CD processes that are quite in line with the requirements of the <span id="ITerm19">Agile methodology</span>. The next chapter introduces Jenkins, a widely used automation server that helps in establishing CI/CD processes.</p></section></div></div></div></div></div></div></section><section _ProgressBarLabels_zgpjq_9 ">29% complete</div></div></div></section></li><li class="_ListItem_17yqw_39" aria-current="false"><section data-testid="toc-part-title-9781484275085-/html/515276_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml" class="_partTitle_cxcpp_1 _subheading_cxcpp_17" aria-current="false"><div class="_titleSection_cxcpp_39"><h5 class="_title_cxcpp_39"><a class="orm-Link-root" href="https://learning.oreilly.com/library/view/ci-cd-pipeline-using/9781484275085/html/515276_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml">2.&nbsp;Introducing
